==Influences and style==
Dutilleux's music extends the legacies of earlier French composers such as [[Claude Debussy|Debussy]] and [[Maurice Ravel|Ravel]] but is also clearly influenced by [[Béla Bartók]] and [[Igor Stravinsky]]. Among his favourite pieces, he mentioned [[Beethoven]]'s [[Late String Quartets (Beethoven)|late string quartets]] and Debussy's ''[[Pelléas et Mélisande (opera)|Pelléas et Mélisande]]''.{{cite web |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YRPsXuQV-l4 |title=Mezzo Voce interview |year=2010 |publisher=Youtube.com|accessdate=2015-11-16}}

-His attitude toward [[serialism]] was more ambiguous. While he always paid attention to the developments of contemporary music and incorporated some serialist techniques into his own compositions,"'Obsessionnel', the third movement of ''Métaboles'', uses a note row. . . ." (Potter 2001), also quoted at [http://www.sospeso.com/contents/composers_artists/dutilleux.html Ensemble Sospeso website]; Nichols and Dutilleux 1994, 87. he also criticized the more radical and intolerant aspects of the movement: "What I reject is the dogma and the authoritarianism which manifested themselves in that period".Nichols and Dutilleux 1994, 87. As an independent composer, Dutilleux always refused to be associated with any school.[http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110609134342/http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf |date=9 June 2011 }} Rather, his works merge the traditions of earlier composers and post-World War II innovations and translate them into his own [[idiosyncratic]] style. His music also contains distant echoes of [[jazz]] as can be heard in the plucked [[double bass]] strings at the very beginning of his First Symphony and his frequent use of [[syncopation|syncopated rhythms]].
+His attitude toward [[serialism]] was more ambiguous. While he always paid attention to the developments of contemporary music and incorporated some serialist techniques into his own compositions,"'Obsessionnel', the third movement of ''Métaboles'', uses a note row. . . ." (Potter 2001), also quoted at [http://www.sospeso.com/contents/composers_artists/dutilleux.html Ensemble Sospeso website]; Nichols and Dutilleux 1994, 87. he also criticized the more radical and intolerant aspects of the movement: "What I reject is the dogma and the authoritarianism which manifested themselves in that period".Nichols and Dutilleux 1994, 87. As an independent composer, Dutilleux always refused to be associated with any school.[http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf] {{wayback|url=http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf |date=20110609134342 |df=y }} Rather, his works merge the traditions of earlier composers and post-World War II innovations and translate them into his own [[idiosyncratic]] style. His music also contains distant echoes of [[jazz]] as can be heard in the plucked [[double bass]] strings at the very beginning of his First Symphony and his frequent use of [[syncopation|syncopated rhythms]].

Dutilleux was greatly enamoured of vocalists, especially the jazz singer [[Sarah Vaughan]] and the great French [[chanson]] singers.{{cite book|author1=Henri Dutilleux|author2=Claude Glayman|title=Henri Dutilleux: Music—mystery and Memory : Conversations with Claude Glayman|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=NVVL66P9ycYC&pg=PA110|accessdate=26 May 2013|year=2003|publisher=Ashgate Publishing, Ltd.|isbn=978-0-7546-0899-8|pages=110–1}}

@@ -45,9 +45,9 @@\n

In his Second Symphony, titled ''Le double'' (1959), the orchestra is divided into two groups: a small one at the front with instruments taken from the various sections (brass, woodwind, strings and percussion) and a bigger one at the back consisting of the rest of the orchestra. Although this brings to mind the [[Baroque]] [[concerto grosso]], the approach is different: in this piece, the smaller ensemble acts as a mirror or ghost of the bigger one, sometimes playing similar or complementary lines, sometimes contrasting ones.Seen and Heard International: [http://www.musicweb-international.com/SandH/2008/Jan-Jun08/dutilleux1602.htm Glyn Pursglove, "Concert Review: Dutilleux, Bartok"], accessed 26 May 2013

-His next work, ''[[Métaboles]]'' (for orchestra, 1965) explores the idea of [[Metamorphosis (biology)|metamorphosis]], how a series of subtle and gradual changes can radically transform a structure. A different section of the orchestra dominates each of the first four movements before the fifth brings them all together for the finale. As a result, it can be considered as a concerto for orchestra.{{cite book|author1=Henri Dutilleux|author2=Claude Glayman|title=Henri Dutilleux: Music—mystery and Memory: Conversations with Claude Glayman|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=NVVL66P9ycYC&pg=PA58|accessdate=26 May 2013|year=2003|publisher=Ashgate Publishing, Ltd.|isbn=978-0-7546-0899-8|page=58}} It quickly achieved celebrity and, following its première by [[George Szell]] and the [[Cleveland Orchestra]], was performed in several North American cities, then in France.CIRM – Centre National de Création Musicale, 2006 "Les Métaboles furent commandées en 1959 par le chef George Szell à Henri Dutilleux à l'occasion du quarantième anniversaire de l'Orchestre de Cleveland, qui en assura la création le 14 janvier 1965 sous la direction du commanditaire. L'œuvre connut rapidement la célébrité et fut reprise dans les grandes villes nord-américaines puis en France." [http://www.cirm-manca.org/fiche-oeuvre.php?oe=68 Métaboles], accessed 26 May 2013 ''Métaboles'' is now one of his most often performed works.{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110716013404/http://www.scenesmagazine.com/spip.php?article300 |date=July 16, 2011 |title=Wasselin 2007 }}
-
-In the 1960s, Dutilleux met [[Mstislav Rostropovich]], who commissioned him to write a [[cello concerto]]. Rostropovich premièred the work, titled ''[[Tout un monde lointain...]]'' [A whole distant world], in 1970. It is one of the most important additions to the cello repertoire of the second half of the 20th century"The great Russian cellist Mstislav Rostropovich commissioned Dutilleux to write Tout un monde lointain, now an important work in the cello repertoire." {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101220090823/http://lso.co.uk/detailedeventinfo&showdetailstype=event&detailID=4597 |date=December 20, 2010 |title=London Symphony Orchestra – 2009 }}"Tout un monde lointain... un des plus beaux concertos pour violoncelle de la seconde moitié du XXe siècle qui... s'est trouvé hissé au premier rang, celui des concertos de Chostakovitch, Penderecki, Britten..." ([http://www.classiquenews.com/applaudir/lire_article.aspx?article=744&identifiant=XKEZOD6G4GPMN2GWGZ41Y6QPI Peters 2007]). and is considered one of the composer's major achievements."In the meantime other cellists had Dutilleux's concerto in their repertoire and several other recordings are now available. Tout un monde lointain... is a splendid work and probably one of the composer's finest achievements"([http://www.musicweb-international.com/classrev/2008/sept08/dutilleux_aecd0861.htm Culot 2008]).
+His next work, ''[[Métaboles]]'' (for orchestra, 1965) explores the idea of [[Metamorphosis (biology)|metamorphosis]], how a series of subtle and gradual changes can radically transform a structure. A different section of the orchestra dominates each of the first four movements before the fifth brings them all together for the finale. As a result, it can be considered as a concerto for orchestra.{{cite book|author1=Henri Dutilleux|author2=Claude Glayman|title=Henri Dutilleux: Music—mystery and Memory: Conversations with Claude Glayman|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=NVVL66P9ycYC&pg=PA58|accessdate=26 May 2013|year=2003|publisher=Ashgate Publishing, Ltd.|isbn=978-0-7546-0899-8|page=58}} It quickly achieved celebrity and, following its première by [[George Szell]] and the [[Cleveland Orchestra]], was performed in several North American cities, then in France.CIRM – Centre National de Création Musicale, 2006 "Les Métaboles furent commandées en 1959 par le chef George Szell à Henri Dutilleux à l'occasion du quarantième anniversaire de l'Orchestre de Cleveland, qui en assura la création le 14 janvier 1965 sous la direction du commanditaire. L'œuvre connut rapidement la célébrité et fut reprise dans les grandes villes nord-américaines puis en France." [http://www.cirm-manca.org/fiche-oeuvre.php?oe=68 Métaboles], accessed 26 May 2013 ''Métaboles'' is now one of his most often performed works.{{Wayback |df=yes|date=20110716013404 |url=http://www.scenesmagazine.com/spip.php?article300 |title=Wasselin 2007 }}
+
+In the 1960s, Dutilleux met [[Mstislav Rostropovich]], who commissioned him to write a [[cello concerto]]. Rostropovich premièred the work, titled ''[[Tout un monde lointain...]]'' [A whole distant world], in 1970. It is one of the most important additions to the cello repertoire of the second half of the 20th century"The great Russian cellist Mstislav Rostropovich commissioned Dutilleux to write Tout un monde lointain, now an important work in the cello repertoire." {{Wayback |df=yes|date=20101220090823 |url=http://lso.co.uk/detailedeventinfo&showdetailstype=event&detailID=4597 |title=London Symphony Orchestra – 2009 }}"Tout un monde lointain... un des plus beaux concertos pour violoncelle de la seconde moitié du XXe siècle qui... s'est trouvé hissé au premier rang, celui des concertos de Chostakovitch, Penderecki, Britten..." ([http://www.classiquenews.com/applaudir/lire_article.aspx?article=744&identifiant=XKEZOD6G4GPMN2GWGZ41Y6QPI Peters 2007]). and is considered one of the composer's major achievements."In the meantime other cellists had Dutilleux's concerto in their repertoire and several other recordings are now available. Tout un monde lointain... is a splendid work and probably one of the composer's finest achievements"([http://www.musicweb-international.com/classrev/2008/sept08/dutilleux_aecd0861.htm Culot 2008]).

After the cello concerto, Dutilleux turned to [[chamber music]] for the first time in more than 20 years and wrote the [[string quartet]] ''[[Ainsi la nuit]]'' (1976). It consists of seven movements, some of which are linked by short "parentheses". The function of these parentheses is to recall material that has already been heard and to introduce fragments that will be fully developed later.Simon Marin's liner notes (Erato CD 0630-14068-2) It is based on a [[hexachord]] (C{{music|sharp}}-G{{music|sharp}}-F-G-C-D) which highlights the intervals of [[perfect fifth|fifth]] and [[major second]].[http://symetrie.com/extraits/isbn_978-2-916738-03-1.pdf] Marie-Delcambe Monpoël, ''La nuit et le temps dans le Quatuor de Dutilleux'' page 94 in ''Henri Dutilleux Entre le cristal et la nuée'' Each movement emphasizes various special effects ([[pizzicato]], [[glissandi]], [[harmonics]], extreme registers, contrasting dynamics...) resulting in a difficult and elaborate work which has been called "one of the treasures of the 20th century quartet repertoire".{{cite web|url=http://rateyourmusic.com/list/rm508/50ish_essential_string_quartets_for_fun_and_profit/ |title=50ish Essential String Quartets for Fun and Profit |publisher=Rate Your Music |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}} He also published various works for piano (''3 Préludes'', ''Figures de résonances'') and ''3 strophes sur le nom de Sacher'' (1976–1982) for solo cello. The latter work was originally composed on the occasion of [[Paul Sacher]]'s 70th birthday in 1976, on a request by the Russian cellist [[Mstislav Rostropovich]] to write compositions for cello solo using his name spelt out in musical notes as the theme eS-A-C-H-E-Re (''Es'' is E-flat in German, ''H'' is B-natural in German, and ''Re'' is D in French; see [[Sacher hexachord]]).

@@ -59,13 +59,13 @@\n

In 2003, he completed ''[[Correspondances]]'', a song-cycle for [[soprano]] and orchestra inspired by poems and letters by [[Prithwindra Mukherjee]], [[Rainer Maria Rilke]], [[Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn]] and [[Vincent van Gogh]]. This work has received a very enthusiastic reception and has been programmed several times since its première."Correspondances... Je suis heureux que cette œuvre soit beaucoup jouée en ce moment, vingt fois dans le monde!" ([http://www.classiquenews.com/applaudir/lire_article.aspx?article=146&identifiant=Y0K57HICUA6C16AQSJX9BVDQT Costantino 2006]).

-His last major work was a song-cycle entitled ''[[Le temps l'horloge]]'',[http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110609134342/http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf |date=9 June 2011 }} written for American soprano [[Renée Fleming]]. It consists of four pieces and an instrumental interlude on two poems by [[Jean Tardieu]], one by [[Robert Desnos]] and one by [[Charles Baudelaire]]. The first three songs were premièred at the [[Saito Kinen Festival Matsumoto]], Japan in September 2007. The American première of this partial version took place in November 2007 with the [[Boston Symphony Orchestra]].[http://www.boston.com/news/globe/living/articles/2007/11/30/henri_dutilleuxs_search_for_lost_time_and_the_clock/ Eichler 2007]. Boston.com (30 November 2007). The complete work was unveiled on 7 May 2009 at the [[Théâtre des Champs-Elysées]] in Paris.{{cite web|url=http://www.concertonet.com/scripts/review.php?ID_review=5584 |title=The Classical Music Network |publisher=ConcertoNet.com |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}{{cite web|url=http://www.lemonde.fr/cgi-bin/ACHATS/acheter.cgi?offre=ARCHIVES&type_item=ART_ARCH_30J&objet_id=1081850&xtmc=dutilleux_enfin_complet&xtcr=3 |title=« Le Temps l'horloge » de Dutilleux, enfin complet |publisher=LeMonde.fr |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}
+His last major work was a song-cycle entitled ''[[Le temps l'horloge]]'',[http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf] {{wayback|url=http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf |date=20110609134342 |df=y }} written for American soprano [[Renée Fleming]]. It consists of four pieces and an instrumental interlude on two poems by [[Jean Tardieu]], one by [[Robert Desnos]] and one by [[Charles Baudelaire]]. Boston.com (30 November 2007). The complete work was unveiled on 7 May 2009 at the [[Théâtre des Champs-Elysées]] in Paris.{{cite web|url=http://www.concertonet.com/scripts/review.php?ID_review=5584 |title=The Classical Music Network |publisher=ConcertoNet.com |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}{{cite web|url=http://www.lemonde.fr/cgi-bin/ACHATS/acheter.cgi?offre=ARCHIVES&type_item=ART_ARCH_30J&objet_id=1081850&xtmc=dutilleux_enfin_complet&xtcr=3 |title=« Le Temps l'horloge » de Dutilleux, enfin complet |publisher=LeMonde.fr |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}

In 2010, Dutilleux added a third movement to his chamber work ''Les Citations''.{{cite news|last=Paulino |first=Romain |title=Henri Dutilleux fêté au Festival d’Auvers-sur-Oise|url=http://www.resmusica.com/2010/06/27/henri-dutilleux-fete/ |accessdate=26 May 2013|newspaper=ResMusica|date=27 June 2010}} The expanded version was premiered at the Festival d’Auvers-sur-Oise.

In 2011, Pascal Gallois transcribed with Dutilleux's approval three of his early vocal works for bassoon and piano: ''Regards sur l'Infini'' (from the early cycle for voice and piano ''Quatre mélodies'') and ''[[Deux sonnets de Jean Cassou]]'' (originally for baritone and piano). He played them in a concert at the Hôtel de Lauzun in presence of the composer.{{cite web|url=http://www.pascalgallois.com/news/Lauzun2011VF.html |title=Pascal Gallois |publisher=Pascal Gallois |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}

-While Dutilleux allowed only a small number of his works to be published, he actually wrote a lot of music but kept only a small fraction of it."This modest output—modest in quantity, though not in quality—is nonetheless deceptive. His biographer Caroline Potter reports, 'Dutilleux has said that, contrary to what may be assumed by glancing at his catalogue, he actually writes a great deal, but uses only a small percentage of the material.{{'"}} ([http://nyphil.org/about-us/the-orchestra/~/media/pdfs/about-us/1213/NYPhilkravisprogramFINALCoverInterior2.ashx The Marie-Josée Kravis Prize for New Music at the New York Philharmonic 2011]) Dutilleux talked several times about his projects and expressed the wish to write more chamber music,"... je voudrais combler les lacunes de mon œuvre ; ce que je n’ai pas fait ou trop peu. Par exemple, j’ai peu d’oeuvres de musique de chambre" ([http://www.classiquenews.com/applaudir/lire_article.aspx?article=146&identifiant=Y0K57HICUA6C16AQSJX9BVDQT Costantino 2006]). notably a second string quartet, a piece for clarinet and ensemble, one for solo double bass as well as some additional piano préludes.{{cite web|author=Bruno Serrou |url=http://brunoserrou.blogspot.be/2013/05/le-grand-compositeur-francais-henri.html |title=Classique d'aujourd'hui, blog d'actualité de la musique classique et contemporaine: Le grand compositeur français Henri Dutilleux est mort |publisher=Brunoserrou.blogspot.be |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}"Nor is the cycle meant as a swan song—the composer has expressed interest in returning to the string quartet genre" ({{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110719164622/http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf |date=July 19, 2011 |title=May 2007 }}){{cite web|url=http://www.altamusica.com/chroniques/index.php?action=MoreDocument&DocRef=5188&DossierRef=4766 |title=La Chronique d'Altamusica |publisher=Altamusica.com |date=2013-05-23 |accessdate=2015-11-16}} He long considered composing an opera but abandoned that project because he could not find a [[libretto]] that appealed to him.
+While Dutilleux allowed only a small number of his works to be published, he actually wrote a lot of music but kept only a small fraction of it."This modest output—modest in quantity, though not in quality—is nonetheless deceptive. His biographer Caroline Potter reports, 'Dutilleux has said that, contrary to what may be assumed by glancing at his catalogue, he actually writes a great deal, but uses only a small percentage of the material.{{'"}} ([http://nyphil.org/about-us/the-orchestra/~/media/pdfs/about-us/1213/NYPhilkravisprogramFINALCoverInterior2.ashx The Marie-Josée Kravis Prize for New Music at the New York Philharmonic 2011]) Dutilleux talked several times about his projects and expressed the wish to write more chamber music,"... je voudrais combler les lacunes de mon œuvre ; ce que je n’ai pas fait ou trop peu. Par exemple, j’ai peu d’oeuvres de musique de chambre" ([http://www.classiquenews.com/applaudir/lire_article.aspx?article=146&identifiant=Y0K57HICUA6C16AQSJX9BVDQT Costantino 2006]). notably a second string quartet, a piece for clarinet and ensemble, one for solo double bass as well as some additional piano préludes.{{cite web|author=Bruno Serrou |url=http://brunoserrou.blogspot.be/2013/05/le-grand-compositeur-francais-henri.html |title=Classique d'aujourd'hui, blog d'actualité de la musique classique et contemporaine: Le grand compositeur français Henri Dutilleux est mort |publisher=Brunoserrou.blogspot.be |date= |accessdate=2015-11-16}}"Nor is the cycle meant as a swan song—the composer has expressed interest in returning to the string quartet genre" ({{Wayback |df=yes|date=20110719164622 |url=http://www.bso.org/images/program_notes/DutilleuxLeTempslHorloge.pdf |title=May 2007 }}){{cite web|url=http://www.altamusica.com/chroniques/index.php?action=MoreDocument&DocRef=5188&DossierRef=4766 |title=La Chronique d'Altamusica |publisher=Altamusica.com |date=2013-05-23 |accessdate=2015-11-16}} He long considered composing an opera but abandoned that project because he could not find a [[libretto]] that appealed to him.

Those who commissioned works from Dutilleux included [[Charles Munch (conductor)|Charles Munch]] (Symphony No. 2, ''Le double''), [[George Szell]] (''Métaboles''), [[Mstislav Rostropovich]] (''Tout un monde lointain'' and ''Timbres, espace, mouvement''), [[Isaac Stern]] (''L'arbre des songes''), [[Anne-Sophie Mutter]] (''Sur le même accord'') and [[Seiji Ozawa]] (''The Shadows of Time'' and ''Le temps l'horloge'').

'''Felice Gimondi''' ({{IPA-it|feˈliːtʃe dʒiˈmondi}}; born 29 September 1942) is an Italian former professional [[racing cyclist]].
-With his 1968 victory at the [[Vuelta a España]], only three years after becoming a professional cyclist, Gimondi, nicknamed "The Phoenix", was the second cyclist (after [[Jacques Anquetil]]) to win all three ''[[Grand Tour (cycling)|Grand Tours]]'' of road cycling: [[Tour de France]] (1965, his first year as a pro), [[Giro d'Italia]] (1967, 1969 and 1976), and [[Vuelta a España]] (1968).[http://www.cyclinghalloffame.com/riders/rider_bio.asp?rider_id=15 Felice Gimondi]. A major [[cyclosportive]] event is named in his honour, the Gran Fondo Felice Gimondi, held annually around Bergamo.

When the [[World War I|First World War]] broke out in August 1914, the [[Royal Northumberland Fusiliers|Northumberland Fusiliers]], a [[fusilier]] [[infantry]] [[regiment]] of the [[British Army]], consisted of 7 [[battalion]]s, eventually expanding to 52 battalions, although not all existed at the same time,{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715140005/http://regiments.org/regiments/uk/inf/005RNF.htm |date=15 July 2007 |title=The Royal Northumberland Fusiliers at regiments.org by T.F.Mills }}{{efn|James' summary{{harvnb|James|1978|loc=Table B, Appendix I to Part II}} shows 51 battalions but does not include the short-lived 38th Battalion.{{harvnb|James|1978|p=47}}}} of which 29 served overseas.{{cite web | url=http://www.northeastmedals.co.uk/british_regiment/northumberland_fusiliers.htm | title=Medals of the Regiments: The Royal Northumberland Fusiliers | publisher=North East Medals | date=2007 | accessdate=18 July 2014 }}{{efn|Battalions that served overseas were [[#1|1st]] and [[#2|2nd]] (Regular), [[#4|1/4th]], [[#5|1/5th]], [[#6|1/6th]], [[#7|1/7th]], [[#2/7|2/7th]] (Territorial), [[#8|8th]], [[#9|9th]], [[#10|10th]], [[#11|11th]], [[#12|12th]], [[#13|13th]], [[#14|14th]], [[#16|16th]], [[#17|17th]], [[#18|18th]], [[#19|19th]] (Service), [[#20|20th]], [[#21|21st]], [[#22|22nd]], [[#23|23rd]] (Service, 1st – 4th Tyneside Scottish), [[#24|24th]], [[#25|25th]], [[#26|26th]], [[#27|27th]] (Service, 1st – 4th Tyneside Irish), [[#36|36th]] (Territorial), [[#1G|1st Garrison]] and [[#2G|2nd Garrison]].}} It was the second largest infantry regiment of the [[British Army during World War I]], surpassed only by the 88 battalions of the [[London Regiment]].{{harvnb|Haythornthwaite|1996|p=219}}{{harvnb|James|1978|loc=Table C, Appendix I to Part II}}

==={{anchor|9}}9th (Northumberland Hussars) Battalion===
-The '''9th (Service) Battalion''' was formed at Newcastle on 8 September 1914 as part of Kitchener's [[Kitchener's Army#Kitchener's Second New Army|Second New Army]]{{snd}}K2{{snd}}and was assigned to the [[52nd Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)|52nd Brigade]], [[17th (Northern) Division]] at [[Wareham, Dorset|Wareham]]. In July 1915 it moved to the [[Western Front (World War I)|Western Front]] where it was to remain until the end of the war. On 3 August 1917, it was transferred to the [[103rd (Tyneside Irish) Brigade|103rd Brigade]], [[34th Division (United Kingdom)|34th Division]].{{cite web | url=http://www.1914-1918.net/34div.htm | title=The 34th Division in 1914–1918 | publisher=The Long, Long Trail | accessdate=9 July 2014 | last=Baker | first=Chris}}{{efn|James says 104th Brigade, 34th Division but this is a mistake as 104th Brigade was never part of the 34th Division.{{harvnb|Becke|1945|pp=44–45}}}} On 25 September 1917, it absorbed the [[2/1st Northumberland Hussars]] and became the '''9th ([[Northumberland Hussars]]) Battalion'''.{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715140005/http://regiments.org/deploy/uk/wf-inf/005-ww1.htm#9 |date=15 July 2007 |title=First World War Hostilities-Only Battalions of The Northumberland Fusiliers 1914–1920 at regiments.org by T.F.Mills }} On 26 May 1918, it was transferred to the [[183rd (2nd Gloucester and Worcester) Brigade|183rd Brigade]], [[61st (2nd South Midland) Division]]. It was disbanded on 1 November 1919 in France. It fought in the following battles with 17th Division:{{harvnb|Becke|1938|pp=76–77}}

==Post-war==
{{anchor|39|40}}The Northumberland Fusiliers continued to raise new battalions after the end of the war: the '''39th (Service) Battalion''' on 10 May 1919 and the '''40th (Service) Battalion''' in September 1919. They were disbanded in France on 5 March 1920 and 19 September 1919, respectively.{{efn|Frederick allows that the 39th and 40th (Service) Battalions may have been disbanded in Egypt on 11 December 1919.}}

-All of the war-raised battalions had been disbanded by the end of March 1920.{{harvnb|Frederick|1984|pp=276–280}} The 1st Line [[Territorial Force]] battalions were reconstituted on 7 February 1920 as part of the new [[Territorial Army (United Kingdom)|Territorial Army]]{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715140005/http://regiments.org/regiments/uk/volmil-england/vinf-no/nd-4.htm |date=15 July 2007 |title=4th Battalion, The Royal Northumberland Fusiliers at regiments.org by T.F.Mills }}{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715140005/http://regiments.org/regiments/uk/volmil-england/vinf-no/nd-5.htm |date=15 July 2007 |title=5th Battalion, The Royal Northumberland Fusiliers at regiments.org by T.F.Mills }}{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715140005/http://regiments.org/regiments/uk/volmil-england/vinf-no/nd-6.htm |date=15 July 2007 |title=6th Battalion, The Royal Northumberland Fusiliers at regiments.org by T.F.Mills }}{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070715140005/http://regiments.org/regiments/uk/volmil-england/vinf-no/nd-7.htm |date=15 July 2007 |title=7th Battalion, The Royal Northumberland Fusiliers at regiments.org by T.F.Mills }} where they once again formed the [[149th (Northumberland) Brigade#Post-war|Northumberland Brigade]] in the [[Northumbrian Division]].{{harvnb|Westlake|1986|p=47}} Therefore, the Northumberland Fusiliers entered the inter-war period with

In November 2011 [[John Lyon (commissioner)|John Lyon]], the [[Parliamentary Commissioner for Standards]] launched an investigation into allegations that Dromey had failed to declare thousands of pounds in salary. Dromey's entry in the register of Members' interests stated he had declined his salary from Unite since entering Parliament. However, in October 2011 he changed his entry to state "Between the General Election and 30 October 2010, I received £27,867 in salary."http://www.birminghampost.net/news/politics-news/2011/11/09/birmingham-mp-jack-dromey-accused-of-not-declaring-union-salary-65233-29743248/ Dromey apologised to the House of Commons on 19 January 2012, in relation to this mistake.

==Marriage and family==
-Dromey married [[Harriet Harman]] in 1982 in the borough of [[London Borough of Brent|Brent]], after meeting her on the picket line of the [[Grunwick dispute]] in 1977; Harman was legal advisor to the Grunwick Strike Committee. They have two sons (born February 1983 and November 1984) and a daughter (born January 1987). Labour colleague [[Patricia Hewitt]] is godmother to one of their children.[http://www.timesonline.co.uk/tol/news/politics/article5780320.ece Profile: Harriet Harman], ''Times Online'', 22 February 2009 The couple decided to send their children to selective schools, the subject of negative comment at the time because it runs counter to Labour Party policy. Dromey served for 10 years on the executive of the [[National Council for Civil Liberties]],{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070721021449/http://www.vulnerableworkers.org.uk/about/commission-members/jack-dromey |date=21 July 2007 |title=Dromey biodata }} a pressure group for which Harman worked as legal officer.{{cite news|url=http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/newstopics/politics/labour/4949555/Harriet-Harman-under-attack-over-bid-to-water-down-child-pornography-law.html|location=London|work=The Daily Telegraph|first=Martin|last=Beckford|title=Harriet Harman under attack over bid to water down child pornography law|date=9 March 2009}}
